01:35:21","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:21","title":"India restricts American Express from adding new customers for violating data storage rules","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2143160","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">India’s central bank has restricted American Express and Diners Club from adding new customers starting next month, it said Friday citing violation of local data-storage rules.</p>\n<p>In a <a href=\"https://rbi.org.in/Scripts/BS_PressReleaseDisplay.aspx?prid=51471\">statement</a>, the Reserve Bank of India said existing customers of either of the two card companies will not be impacted by the new order, which goes into effect May 1.</p>\n<p>This is the first time India’s central bank has penalized any firm for non-compliance with local data storage rules, which was <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/india-data-localisation-exclusive-idINKBN1K20K6\">unveiled in 2018</a>. The rules require payments firms to store all Indian transaction data within servers in the country.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Visa, Mastercard, and several other firms, as well as the U.S. government, have previously requested New Delhi to reconsider its rules, which is designed to allow the regulator “unfettered supervisory access.”</p>\n<p>Visa, Mastercard, and American Express had also lobbied to either significantly change the rules or completely discard it. But after none of those efforts worked, most firms began to comply.</p>\n<p>In a statement Friday evening (local time), an Amex spokesperson said the company was “disappointed that the RBI has this course of action,” but said was working with the authority to resolve the concerns “as quickly as possible.”</p>\n<p>With about 1.5 million customers, American Express has amassed the highest number of customers among foreign banks in India.</p>\n<p>“We have been in regular dialogue with the Reserve Bank of India about data localization requirements and have demonstrated our progress towards complying with the regulation. [&#8230;] This does not impact the services that we offer to our existing customers in India, and our customers can continue to use and accept our cards as normal.”</p>\n<p>Diners Club, which is owned by Discover Financial Services and offers credit cards in India through a partnership with the nation&#8217;s largest private sector bank (HDFC), said in a statement that India remains an important market for the firm and it is working with the central bank to reach a resolution so that it can &#8220;continue to grow in the country.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Last year, India&#8217;s central bank ordered HDFC Bank to not add new credit customers or launch digital businesses after the bank&#8217;s services were hit by a power outage.</p>\n<p>Friday’s order comes as Citigroup, another key foreign bank in India, has announced plans to exit most of its Asian consumer business as it looks to boost its profitability. The consumer operations of the bank in 13 countries is up for sale.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=WlyKw8VDzhY:To6coQNPS3g:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img welcome back to <a href=\"https://open.spotify.com/show/5IEYLip3eDppcOmy5DmphC?si=bjgo57TCQ-uFC38-iTy6HA\">Equity</a>, TechCrunch’s venture capital-focused podcast, where we unpack the numbers behind the headlines.</p>\n<p>First and foremost, Equity was nominated for a Webby for &#8220;Best Technology Podcast&#8221;!!! Drop everything and go <a href=\"https://vote.webbyawards.com/PublicVoting#/2021/podcasts/general-series/technology\">Vote for Equity</a>! We&#8217;d appreciate it. A <em>lot</em>. And even if we lose, well, we&#8217;ll keep doing our thing and making each other laugh.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/nmasc_\">Natasha</a> and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/DannyCrichton\">Danny</a> and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/alex\">Alex</a> and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/cgates123\">Chris</a> got together to chat through the week&#8217;s biggest news. And like every other week in recent memory, it was a busy one. But we did our best to hit some M&#38;A news, some unicorn news and some funding news from smaller startups.</p>\n<p>Now, onto the show rundown; here&#8217;s what we discussed:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>The <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/20/discord-ipo-microsoft-deal/\">Discord-Microsoft deal is done</a>, and Danny has a hot take. Namely, in his view, the deal was mostly banker chatter more than a real possibility. More chaff than wheat, in other words. Agree or not, we&#8217;re stoked for the Discord IPO in a few years (quarters?) time.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/19/mastercard-is-acquiring-identity-verification-company-ekata-for-850m/\">Mastercard bought Erkata</a>, and Danny was on hand to explain why we care about the deal. Sure, it was $825 million in value, but some venture data from <a href=\"https://finledger.com/2021/04/19/mastercard-purchases-identity-verification-company-ekata-its-6th-known-acquisition-to-exceed-a-100m-purchase-price/\">Finledger helped explain just how much capital is flowing into similar companies</a>. Let&#8217;s see how <em>that</em> math works out.</li>\n<li>Clearbanc rebranded itself <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/20/clearbanc-unicorn-clearco/\">into a fintech unicorn,</a> providing services along with sweet, sweet capital.</li>\n<li>The <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/21/a-cooling-trend-in-public-markets-makes-uipaths-down-round-ipo-a-win-for-the-company/\">UiPath IPO finally priced</a> and started to trade. It had a good first day, and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/21/as-uipath-closes-above-its-final-private-valuation-cfo-ashim-gupta-discusses-his-companys-path-to-market/\">you can check out</a> what we learned talking to its CFO here.</li>\n<li>Over in China, a country that we&#8217;ve not covered enough lately, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/20/laiye-rpa-50-million-funding/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">Laiye raised $50 million more</a>. Like UiPath it competes in the RPA world.</li>\n<li>Deel, for one, had a good 2020. It hit 20x growth in revenue last year, and<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/21/remote-hiring-startup-deel-raises-156m-at-a-1-25b-valuation-after-20x-growth-in-2020/\"> recently raised at a $1.25 billion valuation.</a></li>\n<li>And then we closed with two seed rounds raised by recent Y Combinator grads: Here&#8217;s <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/22/queenly-raises-2-3m-for-its-dress-marketplace/\">the Queenly round</a>, and here&#8217;s <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/22/satellite-imagery-startup-albedo-closes-10m-seed-round/\">the Albedo deal</a>!</li>\n</ul>\n<p>We&#8217;ll see you on Monday.</p>\n<div src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/D_Ekn7y0osg\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 23 Apr 2021 14:00:33 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"4f8a04a7699863ec735124c4a83a41be","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn23@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-30-747_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Natasha Mascarenhas","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn23@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-30-747_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn55@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-37-787_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn87@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-37-444_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=D_Ekn7y0osg:ZHl5g_Fp9dg:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn50@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-37-253_bcd58821a05d5482.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=D_Ekn7y0osg:ZHl5g_Fp9dg:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn46@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-37-489_aa16468ec2917688.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn72@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-37-693_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/D_Ekn7y0osg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn22@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-37-236_69a7c9c7d9a38050.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199321632},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:21","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:21","title":"Citi Bike rival JOCO brings shared, docked e-bikes to NYC","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2142693","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Move over Citi Bike, there’s a new docked, shared bike service in town — only this one is all electric. Next week, JOCO will be the first shared operator in New York City to launch a network of e-bike stations on private property for public use.</p>\n<p>The service, powered by shared mobility platform Vulog, will start with 30 stations and 300 e-bikes located around Manhattan, expanding to 100 stations and 1,000 bikes by June. This is not the first new shared operator to hit the streets of New York this year. <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/14/bird-lime-and-veoride-selected-for-nyc-e-scooter-pilot/\">Last week, the city announced the winning companies of the e-scooter pilot in the Bronx</a>. But while Bird, Lime and Veo are restricted to operating in a section of the Bronx, far from any Citi Bike territory, JOCO is under no such constraints.</p>\n<p>The company’s bikes will initially be stationed at parking garages around the city, including at Icon Parking garages, the city’s largest parking operators, but the company says it hopes to expand to residential and commercial buildings in the near future. The company essentially pays landlords to provide this amenity, while absolving them from having to operate or maintain the e-bikes.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>“What differentiates us from Citi Bike is, first of all, our bikes are 100% electric, 100% premium,” co-founder Jonathan “Johnny” Cohen from New York told TechCrunch. (The two co-founders are both named Jonathan Cohen &#8212; one is from New York, the other from London. JOCO&#8230;get it?). “You can reserve our bikes in advance, and as we’re on private property, there is hand sanitizer at our stations, the bikes aren’t getting rained on every night, they’re a bit cleaner and easier to access.”</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"1hQtg0pVJ1\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/14/bird-lime-and-veoride-selected-for-nyc-e-scooter-pilot/\">Bird, Lime and Veo selected for NYC e-scooter pilot</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Bird, Lime and Veo selected for NYC e-scooter pilot&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/14/bird-lime-and-veoride-selected-for-nyc-e-scooter-pilot/embed/#?secret=1hQtg0pVJ1\" data-secret=\"1hQtg0pVJ1\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2142696\" style=\"width: 503px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Frame-1-1-1.png\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2142696\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2142696\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Frame-1-1-1.png?w=493\" alt=\"A map of JOCO's launch e-bike dock locations\" width=\"493\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Frame-1-1-1.png 852w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Frame-1-1-1.png?resize=109,150 109w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Frame-1-1-1.png?resize=218,300 218w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Frame-1-1-1.png?resize=768,1059 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Frame-1-1-1.png?resize=493,680 493w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Frame-1-1-1.png?resize=36,50 36w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 493px) 100vw, 493px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2142696\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">A map of JOCO&#8217;s 30 launch e-bike dock locations in NYC. <strong>Image Credits:</strong> JOCO</p></div></p>\n<p>Citi Bike’s fleet is about 30% electric. To charge the e-bikes, the Lyft-owned company must manually take the drained vehicles from their stations to charge them, whereas JOCO’s vehicles are charged at the stations. Like Citi Bike, each e-bike can last for about 30 miles on a charge.</p>\n<p>“That’s enough to get around Manhattan several times,” said London Jo (another moniker for differentiating between the two Cohens). “We expect our vehicles to always be charged and ready to go for the customer. It defeats the purpose when you’re taking a bike that’s extremely sustainable, and then come along in a gas-burning vehicle to swap the battery. We’re looking to be a truly environmentally friendly company and provide a more consistent and reliable service.”</p>\n<p>Founded in 2019 and funded privately by a group of former CEOs of Fortune 500 companies, and specifically investors with technology and real estate backgrounds, JOCO offers e-bikes at a price point that’s comparable, if not directly competitive, to Citi Bike. It’ll cost riders $1 to unlock the bike and .25 cents a minute, so a 10 minute ride will come out to $3.50. If you can find an electric Citi Bike, it’ll cost a rider $3.50 to unlock and .18 cents a minute, which comes out to about $5.30.</p>\n<p>“That’s significantly cheaper in our opinion for a brand new, gorgeous, full-electric premium bike,” said NY Jo.</p>\n<p>Neither company charges unlock fees for members. JOCO’s monthly membership is $49 per month with unlimited use, and Citi Bike’s is $20 per month, with monthly members continuing to pay 18 cents per minute, and annual members paying 12 cents per minute. Under Citi Bike’s annual membership, if a rider is averaging out about five 10-minute rides per week, the monthly spend is comparable between the two companies.</p>\n<p>“Citi Bike has been around since 2013 and has done a tremendous job at driving cycling adoption on the streets of NYC,” Monica Wejman, Vulog’s North America managing director, told TechCrunch. “And now you have JOCO entering this space, powered by Vulog, really there to complement Citi Bike and satisfy what we’re seeing as a significant increase in demand for access to e-bikes. We’re truly empowering mobility operators to launch mobility programs at scale.”</p>\n<p>While JOCO will not be reliant on the NYC Department of Transportation to carve out street and sidewalk space for docking stations, the operator is still taking steps to ensure a good working relationship with the city.</p>\n<p>London Jo says JOCO’s bikes are made with safety-critical features, like hidden cables to make them less susceptible to vandalism, puncture-proof airless tires and bike-tracking, provided by Vulog’s backend.</p>\n<p>“In addition, by operating in private spaces, we’re eliminating that problem of sidewalk clutter for the city,” said the British Cohen. “And they don’t have to worry about what has to go to fit 50 new bikes on the street. We’re taking a big headache off them, and it’s allowing us to stay in control a little bit more and not have to depend on the city.”</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"8TxN4Lxx4E\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/20/why-micromobility-is-poised-to-come-out-of-the-pandemic-stronger-than-before/\">Why micromobility may emerge from the pandemic stronger than before</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Why 01:35:21","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:21","title":"After going public, once-hot startups are riding a valuation roller coaster","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2142960","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">To close out the week, a short meditation on value, or, more precisely, how assets are valued in today&#8217;s markets.</p>\n<p>Do you recall the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/06/coinbases-monster-q1-in-context/\">pre-direct-listing hype</a> Coinbase enjoyed? After reporting its estimated first-quarter financial performance, interest in the domestic cryptocurrency trading giant ran red-hot.</p>\n<p>When Coinbase set a $250 per-share direct listing <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/13/coinbase-sets-direct-listing-reference-price-at-250-share-valuing-the-company-at-as-much-as-65b/\">reference price</a>, it was broadly viewed as modest, if not downright low. Of course, a reference price is just that &#8212; a reference &#8212; so it wasn&#8217;t too big a deal. But it also wasn&#8217;t surprising that Coinbase shares traded as high as $429.54 on their first day, according to <a href=\"https://finance.yahoo.com/quote/COIN/history?p=COIN\">Yahoo Finance data</a>.</p>\n<p>Coinbase equity hasn&#8217;t topped $400 in any following day and is now under the $300 mark, with more declines set to arrive as trading commences. Its reference price looms, and suddenly a price that felt intensely conservative before Coinbase began to trade is starting to look nearly reasonable.</p>\n<hr />\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><strong><em>The Exchange explores startups, markets and money.  </em></strong></p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><strong><em>Read it <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/subscribe/?tpcc=theexchange\">every morning on Extra Crunch</a> or get <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/newsletters\">The Exchange newsletter</a> every Saturday.</em></strong></p>\n<hr />\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/subscribe/?tpcc=theexchange\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignright wp-image-1995213 size-medium\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?w=300\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg 900w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=300,300 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=768,768 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=680,680 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></a>There have been other notable declines in value among some recently public, more technologically differentiated companies. The Exchange has watched with something akin to polite confusion as the value of Root, a neoinsurance company, fell to a third of its public-market highs <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/28/3-lessons-from-roots-ipo-pricing/\">after going public</a>, even though it <a href=\"https://seekingalpha.com/news/3666921-root-eps-misses-0_07-beats-on-revenue\">beat growth expectations</a> in its most recent quarterly report.</p>\n<p>We could toss UiPath into our trend of wildly meandering value. The company&#8217;s initial IPO price range targeted a price <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/12/uipaths-first-ipo-pricing-could-be-a-warning-to-late-stage-investors/\">as low as $43 per share</a>. Today it&#8217;s worth $76.75 per share in pre-market trading.</p>\n<p>No one knows what anything is worth, again. This is the feeling I get while watching the markets work to determine how to value assets as diverse as startups crossing the private-public divide to the value of Bitcoin, which was supposed to keep going up. Until it suddenly reversed gear.</p>\n<p>Frankly, we&#8217;re still dealing with new-enough models &#8212; or big-enough guesses about the future baked into business models &#8212; that it&#8217;s hard to really value the most uncertain (and therefore most exciting) companies, let alone cryptocurrencies. live","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2142641","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><iframe class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/lW07SN3YoLI?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;fs=1&#038;hl=en-US&#038;autohide=2&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;' sandbox='allow-scripts allow-same-origin allow-popups allow-presentation'></iframe></p>\n<p>SpaceX is set to launch its second operational commercial crew mission to the International Space Station for NASA, with a liftoff time of 5:49 AM EDT (2:49 AM PDT) on Friday morning. The flight will carry four astronauts, including two from NASA, one from JAXA (the Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency) and one from the ESA (European Space Agency), to the station, where they will begin a regular tour of duty conducting science experiments and maintaining and upgrading the orbital platform.</p>\n<p>This is the second commercial crew mission for SpaceX, which officially <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/02/spacex-and-nasa-successfully-return-crew-dragon-spacecraft-to-earth-with-astronauts-on-board/\">qualified its Dragon spacecraft and Falcon 9 rocket for human flight last year</a>. NASA then launched four astronauts using <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/15/spacex-and-nasa-successfully-launch-four-astronauts-to-space-for-first-operational-dragon-crew-mission/\">SpaceX&#8217;s human-certified launch system later that year in November</a>, becoming the first private company to deliver people to the ISS, and the first American vehicle to do so since the retirement of the Space Shuttle in 2011. Since the end of that program, NASA has relied on buying rides aboard Russian Soyuz rockets to keep up its representation on the ISS.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>There&#8217;s already a SpaceX Crew Dragon at the Space Station from that Crew-1 launch last year, and it was relocated to another port on the station earlier this month in preparation for the arrival of the one flying for Crew-2. The Crew-1 Dragon capsule is set to return to Earth with astronauts on board once they&#8217;re relieved by this flight&#8217;s crew, likely later this month on April 28.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Mb5rBb2V5t\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/15/spacex-and-nasa-successfully-launch-four-astronauts-to-space-for-first-operational-dragon-crew-mission/\">SpaceX and NASA successfully launch four astronauts to space for first operational Dragon crew mission</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;SpaceX and NASA successfully launch four astronauts to space for first operational Dragon crew mission&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/15/spacex-and-nasa-successfully-launch-four-astronauts-to-space-for-first-operational-dragon-crew-mission/embed/#?secret=Mb5rBb2V5t\" data-secret=\"Mb5rBb2V5t\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>One major notable change for this launch is the use of a flight-proven Falcon 9 rocket booster. SpaceX has previously used new boosters fresh from the factory for its human launches, though it has a spotless track record when it comes to booster re-use for its cargo flights. It&#8217;s also the first re-use of a dragon spacecraft, and both components of this launch system actually previously supported human launches, with the first stage serving during Crew-1, and the Dragon capsule providing the ride for Demo-2, which flew astronauts Bob Behnken and Doug Hurley.</p>\n<p>The astronauts on today&#8217;s flight are Shane Kimbrough and Megan McArthur from NASA, as well as Akihiko Hoshide from JAXA and Thomas Pesquet from the ESA. As mentioned, liftoff time is set for 5:49 AM EDT, but SpaceX will begin streaming live hours in advance at approximately 1:30 AM EDT on Friday (10:30 PM PDT on Thursday).</p>\n<div class=\"embed Etherington","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn23@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-30-747_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn55@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-37-787_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn87@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-37-444_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=mA7QIBT_Wek:8zu0aiHvOao:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn31@2020_4/2021/04/23/17-35-37-260_b35408d79f7346f1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=mA7QIBT_Wek:8zu0aiHvOao:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn70@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-37-265_b3df0b06309797c3.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn72@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-37-693_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/mA7QIBT_Wek":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn11@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-37-689_e4c5b569ea2cf19d.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199321613},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:21","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:21","title":"Deepfake tech takes on satellite maps","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2142553","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">While the concept of &#8220;deepfakes,&#8221; or AI-generated synthetic imagery, has been decried primarily in connection with involuntary depictions of people, the technology is dangerous (and interesting) in other ways as well. For instance, researchers have shown that it can be used to manipulate satellite imagery to produce real-looking — but totally fake — overhead maps of cities.</p>\n<p>The study, <a href=\"https://www.washington.edu/news/2021/04/21/a-growing-problem-of-deepfake-geography-how-ai-falsifies-satellite-images/\">led by Bo Zhao from the University of Washington</a>, is not intended to alarm anyone but rather to show the risks and opportunities involved in applying this rather infamous technology to cartography. In fact their approach has as much in common with &#8220;style transfer&#8221; techniques — redrawing images in an impressionistic, crayon and arbitrary other fashions — than with deepfakes as they are commonly understood.</p>\n<p>The team trained a machine learning system on satellite images of three different cities: Seattle, nearby Tacoma and Beijing. Each has its own distinctive look, just as a painter or medium does. For instance, Seattle tends to have larger overhanging greenery and narrower streets, while Beijing is more monochrome and — in the images used for the study — the taller buildings cast long, dark shadows. The system learned to associate details of a street map (like Google or Apple&#8217;s) with those of the satellite view.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The resulting machine learning agent, when given a street map, returns a realistic-looking faux satellite image of what that area would look like if it were in any of those cities. In the following image, the map corresponds to the top right satellite image of Tacoma, while the lower versions show how it might look in Seattle and Beijing.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2142604\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Zhao-deepfake-geography-fig-4.png\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2142604\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2142604\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Zhao-deepfake-geography-fig-4.png\" alt=\"Four images show a street map and a real satellite image of Tacoma, and two simulated satellite images of the same streets in Seattle and Beijing.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"1082\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Zhao-deepfake-geography-fig-4.png 1226w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Zhao-deepfake-geography-fig-4.png?resize=142,150 142w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Zhao-deepfake-geography-fig-4.png?resize=284,300 284w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Zhao-deepfake-geography-fig-4.png?resize=768,811 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Zhao-deepfake-geography-fig-4.png?resize=644,680 644w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Zhao-deepfake-geography-fig-4.png?resize=47,50 47w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2142604\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Zhao et al.</p></div></p>\n<p>A close inspection will show that the fake maps aren&#8217;t as sharp as the real one, and there are probably some logical inconsistencies like streets that go nowhere and the like. But at a glance the Seattle and Beijing images are perfectly plausible.</p>\n<p>One only has to think for a few minutes to conceive of uses for fake maps like this, both legitimate and otherwise. The researchers suggest that the technique could be used to simulate imagery of places for which no satellite imagery is available — like one of these cities in the days before such things were possible, or for a planned expansion or zoning change. The system doesn&#8217;t have to imitate another place altogether — it could be trained on a more densely populated part of the same city, or one with wider streets.</p>\n<p>It could conceivably even be used, <a href=\"https://spectrum.ieee.org/tech-talk/artificial-intelligence/machine-learning/ai-ancient-maps-satellite-images\">as this rather more whimsical project was</a>, to make realistic-looking modern maps from ancient hand-drawn ones.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"GZXJia1KHP\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/23/deep-science-alzheimers-screening-forest-mapping-drones-machine-learning-in-space-more/\">Deep Science: Alzheimer&#8217;s screening, forest-mapping drones, machine learning in space, more</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Deep Science: Alzheimer&#8217;s screening, forest-mapping drones, machine learning in space, more&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/23/deep-science-alzheimers-screening-forest-mapping-drones-machine-learning-in-space-more/embed/#?secret=GZXJia1KHP\" data-secret=\"GZXJia1KHP\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Should technology like this be bent to less constructive purposes, the paper also looks at ways to detect such simulated imagery using careful examination of colors and features.</p>\n<p>The work challenges the general assumption of the &#8220;absolute reliability of satellite images or other geospatial data,&#8221; said Zhao in a UW news article, and certainly as with other media that kind thinking has to go by the wayside as new threats appear. You can read the full paper at the journal <a href=\"https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1080/15230406.2021.1910075?journalCode=tcag20\">Cartography and Geographic Information Science</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=cTzDlWtxnt0:nRzMey-yA5c:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/cTzDlWtxnt0\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 22 Apr 2021 20:46:12 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Zhao-deepfake-geography-fig-4.png","linkMd5":"6958025294b2965f513bd296b86e4d44","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn20@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-36-578_ee19066839458e81.webp","destWidth":1226,"destHeight":1295,"sourceBytes":3072443,"destBytes":121032,"author":"Devin Coldewey","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Zhao-deepfake-geography-fig-4.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn20@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-36-578_ee19066839458e81.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn23@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-30-747_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn55@2020_5/2021/04/23/17-35-37-787_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn87@2020_2/2021/04/23/17-35-37-444_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=cTzDlWtxnt0:nRzMey-yA5c:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn100@2020_3/2021/04/23/17-35-37-576_8d1486b587ffb8f9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=cTzDlWtxnt0:nRzMey-yA5c:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn19@2020_6/2021/04/23/17-35-37-259_ea2fcbcc1ffad201.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn72@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-37-693_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/cTzDlWtxnt0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn64@2020_1/2021/04/23/17-35-37-273_af4ecc40bc243bbe.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1619199321616},{"createdTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:21","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:21","title":"Hyundai invests in teleoperations startup Ottopia as part of $9M round","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2142983","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">After spending much of his career in mission-critical environments, including the Israeli Air Force, Israeli Intelligence and leading development of a cybersecurity product at Microsoft, Amit Rosenzweig turned his attention to autonomous vehicles.</p>\n<p>It was a technology <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">that he soon recognized would need what every other mission-critical system requires: humans. </span></p>\n<p>&#8220;I understood that there are so many edge cases that will not be solved purely by AI and machine learning, and there must be some kind of human-in-the-loop intervention,&#8221; Rosenzweig said in a recent interview. &#8220;You don&#8217;t have any mission-critical system on the planet — not nuclear power plants, not airplanes — without human supervision. A human must be in the loop or present in some way for autonomous mobility to exist, even in 10 or probably 20 years from now.&#8221;</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>That &#8220;human in the loop&#8221; conclusion led Rosenzweig to found teleoperations startup <a href=\"https://ottopia.tech/\">Ottopia</a> in 2018. (His brother, Oren Rosenzweig is also in the autonomous vehicle business via the lidar company he co-founded, Innoviz.) Ottopia&#8217;s first product is a universal teleoperation platform that allows a human operator to monitor and control any type of vehicle from thousands of miles away. Ottopia&#8217;s software is combined with off-the-shelf hardware components like monitors and cameras to create a teleoperations center. The company&#8217;s software also includes assistive features, which provide &#8220;path&#8221; instructions to the AV without having to remotely control the vehicle.</p>\n<p>Since launching, the small 25-person company has racked up investors and partners such as BMW, fixed-route AV startup <a href=\"https://maymobility.com/\">May Mobility</a> and <a href=\"https://bestmile.com/\">Bestmile</a>. Ottopia said Friday that it has raised $9 million from Hyundai Motor Group as well as Maven and IN Venture, the Israel-focused venture capital arm of Sumitomo Corporation. Existing investors MizMaa and Israeli firm NextGear also participated.</p>\n<p>Hyundai and IN Venture also gained board seats. Woongjun Jang, who heads up Hyundai&#8217;s autonomous driving center, and IN Venture managing partner Eyal Rosner, are now on Ottopia&#8217;s board.</p>\n<p>Ottopia has raised a total of $12 million to date, and Rosenzweig has already set his sights on a larger round to help fund the company&#8217;s growth.</p>\n<p>For now, Rosenzweig is focused on doubling his workforce to 50 people by the end of the year and opening an office in the United States. Rosenzweig said the company is also expanding into other applications of its teleoperations software, including defense, mining and logistics. However, most of Ottopia&#8217;s resources will continue to be dedicated to automotive, and specifically the deployment of autonomous cars, trucks and shuttles.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The motivation is really simple — it&#8217;s simple but it&#8217;s hard to do — and that&#8217;s to make affordable autonomous transportation closer to reality,&#8221; Rosenzweig said. &#8220;The problem of course is that when an AV does not have any kind of backup or any kind of safety net in the form of teleoperations and it gets stuck, passengers are going to get anxious, &#8216;what&#8217;s going on, why, why is this not moving&#8217;.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The other problem, Rosenzweig noted, is that AVs need to be combined with an efficient transit service. That&#8217;s where he sees his newest partner, on-demand shuttle and transit software company Via, coming in.</p>\n<p>Under the partnership, which was also announced this week, Via will offer autonomous vehicle fleets that combine its fleet management software with Ottopia&#8217;s teleoperations platform. Via is not developing its own self-driving software system. In November 2020, Via <a href=\"https://maymobility.com/may-mobility-and-via-announce-partnership-that-will-integrate-on-demand-avs-into-public-transit/\">announced it had partnered</a> with May Mobility to launch an autonomous vehicle platform that integrates on-demand shared rides, public transportation and transit options for passengers with accessibility needs.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"t0HxVdd2Hk\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/07/26/ethics-in-the-age-of-autonomous-vehicles/\">Ethics in the age of autonomous vehicles</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Ethics in the age of autonomous vehicles&#8221; class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\tRyan Craig is managing director of <a href=\"https://www.achievepartners.com/\">Achieve Partners</a>, an investment firm focused at the intersection of education and employment, and author of “A New U: Faster + Cheaper Alternatives to College.”\t</div>\n\t\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__more-articles\">\n\t\t<span class=\"more-articles-title\">More posts by this contributor</span>\n\t\t<ul class=\"more-articles-list\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/09/05/the-new-marketplaces-connecting-school-and-work/\">The new marketplaces connecting school and work</a></li>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/07/28/last-mile-training-and-the-future-of-work-in-an-expanding-gig-economy/\">Last-mile training and the future of work in an expanding gig economy</a></li>\n\t\t\t\t\t</ul>\n\t</div>\n\t</div>\n</div><p id=\"speakable-summary\">You can always tell a system is broken when you change the inputs and the outcomes don’t improve. Any software engineer will tell you that.</p>\n<p>Using this metric, it’s clear the United States’ antiquated higher education system is truly broken. Overpriced and underperforming, the system is failing on two key fronts: addressing racial inequalities and closing our country’s growing tech skills gaps.</p>\n<p>For all the changes made to the system to welcome people of color into the classroom, the outcomes in terms of wealth, equity distribution and representation are worse than ever.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>On average, Black college graduates <a href=\"https://urldefense.proofpoint.com/v2/url?u=https-3A__educationdata.org_student-2Dloan-2Ddebt-2Dby-2Drace-23-3A-7E-3Atext-3DBlack-2520and-2520African-2520American-2520college-2C12.5-2525-2520more-2520than-2520they-2520borrowed.&#38;d=DwMFaQ&#38;c=euGZstcaTDllvimEN8b7jXrwqOf-v5A_CdpgnVfiiMM&#38;r=aJN_B9lxV3XtoOYQqya_Bpi9ZKtvuy549O8avEZxzXs&#38;m=Rc7R0N-0O8dJS1R0h99qNS10uYJA1v_dXeFVdgp71fE&#38;s=AgesAfh0oJkgBMSpAUegyKEm_zBMmhVJauFgRHPk6_o&#38;e=\">owe $25,000 more in student debt</a> than their white peers. Worse still, four years after throwing their caps in the air, 48% of Black graduates owe an average of <a href=\"https://urldefense.proofpoint.com/v2/url?u=https-3A__educationdata.org_student-2Dloan-2Ddebt-2Dby-2Drace-23-3A-7E-3Atext-3DBlack-2520and-2520African-2520American-2520college-2C12.5-2525-2520more-2520than-2520they-2520borrowed.&#38;d=DwMFaQ&#38;c=euGZstcaTDllvimEN8b7jXrwqOf-v5A_CdpgnVfiiMM&#38;r=aJN_B9lxV3XtoOYQqya_Bpi9ZKtvuy549O8avEZxzXs&#38;m=Rc7R0N-0O8dJS1R0h99qNS10uYJA1v_dXeFVdgp71fE&#38;s=AgesAfh0oJkgBMSpAUegyKEm_zBMmhVJauFgRHPk6_o&#38;e=\">12.5% more than they borrowed in the first place</a>.</p>\n<p>A labor market built on degree requirements has little hope of correcting course.</p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--right\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\tWhile colleges and universities do as good a job as they’ve ever done at preparing students with the cognitive and critical thinking skills they’ll need to be successful in the long run, the college system just isn’t providing the right training for jobs in 2021.\t\t\t\t\t</blockquote>\n\t</div>\n\t</p>\n<p>Looking past the college experience, the unemployment rate for Black Americans stands at <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/news.release/empsit.t02.htm\">nearly 10%</a>, compared with 5.5% for white Americans, while the typical Black American family has<a href=\"https://www.federalreserve.gov/econres/notes/feds-notes/disparities-in-wealth-by-race-and-ethnicity-in-the-2019-survey-of-consumer-finances-20200928.htm\"> eight times less wealth</a> than a white family. This is coupled with the fact that Black people make up just <a href=\"https://urldefense.proofpoint.com/v2/url?u=https-3A__www.issgovernance.com_library_2019-2Dus-2Dboard-2Ddiversity-2Dtrends_&#38;d=DwMFaQ&#38;c=euGZstcaTDllvimEN8b7jXrwqOf-v5A_CdpgnVfiiMM&#38;r=aJN_B9lxV3XtoOYQqya_Bpi9ZKtvuy549O8avEZxzXs&#38;m=Rc7R0N-0O8dJS1R0h99qNS10uYJA1v_dXeFVdgp71fE&#38;s=PfcAR6_TIWImSrTh9QiOLvKp787HGKVfd0FMfp8tHg4&#38;e=\">4.1% of Russell 3000 board members</a> &#8212; compared to 13.4% of the population.</p>\n<p>This isn’t just a matter of grave injustice. The racial wealth gap costs the U.S. economy<a href=\"https://www.mckinsey.com/industries/public-and-social-sector/our-insights/the-economic-impact-of-closing-the-racial-wealth-gap\"> $1 trillion to $1.5 trillion </a>in GDP output each year. There is a financial and moral imperative to do something about it.</p>\n<p>Then there’s the skills gaps: For all the belated changes made to academic programs and curricula, and while colleges and universities do as good a job as they’ve ever done at preparing students with the cognitive and critical thinking skills they’ll need to be successful in the long run, the college system just isn’t providing the right training for jobs in 2021. Ten years ago, <a href=\"https://urldefense.proofpoint.com/v2/url?u=https-3A__www.pwc.com_gx_en_ceo-2Dsurvey_2019_Theme-2Dassets_reports_talent-2Dtrends-2Dreport.pdf&#38;d=DwMFaQ&#38;c=euGZstcaTDllvimEN8b7jXrwqOf-v5A_CdpgnVfiiMM&#38;r=aJN_B9lxV3XtoOYQqya_Bpi9ZKtvuy549O8avEZxzXs&#38;m=Rc7R0N-0O8dJS1R0h99qNS10uYJA1v_dXeFVdgp71fE&#38;s=Px6UX8tOH7wrQTn-nDiQhQ_BiFfHZT46JXgDZAHnYbA&#38;e=\">56% of CEOs were “extremely” or “somewhat” concerned by the lack of talent for digital roles</a>. By 2019, this had <a href=\"https://urldefense.proofpoint.com/v2/url?u=https-3A__www.pwc.com_gx_en_ceo-2Dsurvey_2019_Theme-2Dassets_reports_talent-2Dtrends-2Dreport.pdf&#38;d=DwMFaQ&#38;c=euGZstcaTDllvimEN8b7jXrwqOf-v5A_CdpgnVfiiMM&#38;r=aJN_B9lxV3XtoOYQqya_Bpi9ZKtvuy549O8avEZxzXs&#38;m=Rc7R0N-0O8dJS1R0h99qNS10uYJA1v_dXeFVdgp71fE&#38;s=Px6UX8tOH7wrQTn-nDiQhQ_BiFfHZT46JXgDZAHnYbA&#38;e=\">jumped to 79%</a>. This is why well <a href=\"https://www.burning-glass.com/wp-content/uploads/permanent_detour_underemployment_report.pdf\">over 50% of new and recent graduates are underemployed</a> in their first jobs out of college (two-thirds of whom will be underemployed five years later, and half a decade later).</p>\n<p>There must be a better way. A way that empowers young people to achieve in-demand skills while avoiding the decades-long burden of student loans. A way that doesn’t discriminate based on socioeconomic background while exposing talent-hungry employers to a new pool of qualified, driven individuals.</p>\n<p>In the explosion of edtech businesses with new approaches, we are in danger of overlooking an established model that can be adapted to solve these challenges. That model is apprenticeships.</p>\n<h2>The apprenticeship movement</h2>\n<p>There’s a lingering perception in America that apprenticeships are the province of construction and building trades, or even medieval guilds like smithing and glass-blowing. Well, not anymore. While we’ve been focused on edtech, or despairing over the widening skills gap, apprenticeships have been rebooted. Modern, tech-driven apprenticeships are emerging as a faster, cheaper and more impactful alternative to higher education.</p>\n<p>In Europe, tech companies — and nontech companies <a href=\"https://fortune.com/2021/02/02/ibm-salaries-jobs-training-new-collar-covid-economy/\">increasingly hiring entry-level workers</a> with discrete tech skills — are already leveraging<a href=\"https://fortune.com/2021/02/02/ibm-salaries-jobs-training-new-collar-covid-economy/\"> apprenticeships</a> to provide a direct route into the labor market for diverse talent. From software engineers to data analysts, the apprentice of the 21st century is as likely to wield a keyboard as a wrench.</p>\n<p>Fully employed from day one, apprentices earn a wage while they learn on a program that is entirely free to the individual. Their training is delivered alongside their role, with this applied learning approach ensuring relevant skills are tested and embedded right away.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"iz2bt8UmN9\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/01/28/12-investors-say-lifelong-learning-is-taking-edtech-mainstream/\">13 investors say lifelong learning is taking edtech mainstream</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;13 investors say lifelong learning is taking edtech mainstream&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/01/28/12-investors-say-lifelong-learning-is-taking-edtech-mainstream/embed/#?secret=iz2bt8UmN9\" data-secret=\"iz2bt8UmN9\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Part of the challenge presented by the existing system is that college provides a single shot of learning at the start of a career, with a focus on knowledge rather than skills. Instead of time-consuming traditional education models, we should be encouraging companies to focus on training individuals for highly skilled jobs and adapting training as roles shift through a lifelong learning journey.</p>\n<p>Against a college system churning out graduates armed with knowledge of limited applicability in the workplace, apprentices have real-work experience and transferable skill sets in the tech and digital spaces.</p>\n<p>As we write this, tech <a href=\"https://urldefense.proofpoint.com/v2/url?u=https-3A__www.dol.gov_agencies_eta_apprenticeship_about_statistics&#38;d=DwMFaQ&#38;c=euGZstcaTDllvimEN8b7jXrwqOf-v5A_CdpgnVfiiMM&#38;r=aJN_B9lxV3XtoOYQqya_Bpi9ZKtvuy549O8avEZxzXs&#38;m=Rc7R0N-0O8dJS1R0h99qNS10uYJA1v_dXeFVdgp71fE&#38;s=lh-GS1bPsHrzsbzOgSkhYGdgop6VmM2MpUREk013alE&#38;e=\">apprenticeships represent less than 1% of American apprenticeships </a>, while <a href=\"https://urldefense.proofpoint.com/v2/url?u=https-3A__www.dol.gov_agencies_eta_apprenticeship_about_statistics&#38;d=DwMFaQ&#38;c=euGZstcaTDllvimEN8b7jXrwqOf-v5A_CdpgnVfiiMM&#38;r=aJN_B9lxV3XtoOYQqya_Bpi9ZKtvuy549O8avEZxzXs&#38;m=Rc7R0N-0O8dJS1R0h99qNS10uYJA1v_dXeFVdgp71fE&#38;s=lh-GS1bPsHrzsbzOgSkhYGdgop6VmM2MpUREk013alE&#38;e=\">78% of apprentices are white</a>. But change is in the air. In recent weeks, the Biden administration has gone out of its way to highlight tech as a growth area for apprenticeships.</p>\n<p>The president also announced <a href=\"https://urldefense.proofpoint.com/v2/url?u=https-3A__www.whitehouse.gov_briefing-2Droom_statements-2Dreleases_2021_02_17_fact-2Dsheet-2Dbiden-2Dadministration-2Dto-2Dtake-2Dsteps-2Dto-2Dbolster-2Dregistered-2Dapprenticeships_&#38;d=DwMFaQ&#38;c=euGZstcaTDllvimEN8b7jXrwqOf-v5A_CdpgnVfiiMM&#38;r=aJN_B9lxV3XtoOYQqya_Bpi9ZKtvuy549O8avEZxzXs&#38;m=Rc7R0N-0O8dJS1R0h99qNS10uYJA1v_dXeFVdgp71fE&#38;s=iRWri3Hob0ohVZ8HwRyyF3b9musmHkEyUmPWiFdtUlo&#38;e=\">his commitment to raising apprenticeship standards</a>, starting with casting off industry-recognized apprenticeship programs lacking in quality and training rigor.</p>\n<p>These aren’t just words, either. The apprenticeship reboot will be powered by a new <a href=\"https://www.congress.gov/bill/117th-congress/house-bill/447\">National Apprenticeship Act </a>. This proposed legislation commits $3 billion over the next five years to expanding registered apprenticeship programs across a range of industries. If it’s done right, tech will be front and center.</p>\n<h2>The benefit to businesses</h2>\n<p>All this is welcome good news for businesses desperate to close skills gaps. As roles evolve at an ever-faster pace, it’s becoming more and more difficult to know what a college degree actually says about an individual’s ability. Yes, they went to a “good” school. But when <a href=\"https://www.marketwatch.com/story/half-of-young-americans-say-college-isnt-necessary-2019-08-06\">half of Americans say their degree is irrelevant to their current role</a>, how does prestige translate to jobs, let alone ability to perform in the workplace?</p>\n<p>Increasingly operating in the dark, tech businesses and nontech managers hiring for tech roles are competing with each other to poach experienced talent into senior roles. It’s continuing to fish in a very limited, homogeneous pool and an expensive short-term solution.</p>\n<p>Professional apprenticeships allow business leaders to be more strategic and proactive in their hiring practices. They can mold apprentices to the roles they actually need to fill while focusing on their organization’s specific requirements. It beats relying on uniform, outdated education models.</p>\n<p>Better still, by training apprentices from the start of their career, companies inspire loyalty and eliminate the tricky transition phase recent grads and external hires usually need. Once converted to full-time employees, apprentices tend to persist for twice as long as traditional direct hires.</p>\n<p>While skills gaps are created by the future racing toward us, racial inequalities are rooted in our past. Professional apprenticeships help break down entrenched structural barriers to careers in industries like tech.</p>\n<p>Most important, they look beyond the degree requirements that screen out 67% of Black and 79% of Hispanic Americans. Because apprenticeships are paid pathways to economic opportunity, they truly level the playing field and allow companies to make genuine advances toward racial equality &#8212; beyond a few neatly crafted Instagram posts. Meanwhile, by tapping into diverse talent pools early, businesses can develop individuals and build real, recognizable routes to the boardroom.</p>\n<p>They would be right, too. A 2020 report by McKinsey found companies with the highest diversity <a href=\"https://urldefense.proofpoint.com/v2/url?u=https-3A__www.mckinsey.com_business-2Dfunctions_organization_our-2Dinsights_why-2Ddiversity-2Dmatters&#38;d=DwMFaQ&#38;c=euGZstcaTDllvimEN8b7jXrwqOf-v5A_CdpgnVfiiMM&#38;r=aJN_B9lxV3XtoOYQqya_Bpi9ZKtvuy549O8avEZxzXs&#38;m=Rc7R0N-0O8dJS1R0h99qNS10uYJA1v_dXeFVdgp71fE&#38;s=nkaIrANwm3SsODk5tOu6CCoL5GD9gNjXTD2GnkuxMPo&#38;e=\">earned 35% more than their industry average</a>. Similarly, the share returns of the most diverse companies in the S&#38;P 500 outperformed the least diverse by a staggering 240%.</p>\n<p>The time for change is now. According to the National Center for Education Statistics, <a href=\"https://urldefense.proofpoint.com/v2/url?u=https-3A__www.insidehighered.com_quicktakes_2020_02_18_41-2Drecent-2Dgrads-2Dwork-2Djobs-2Dnot-2Drequiring-2Ddegree&#38;d=DwMFaQ&#38;c=euGZstcaTDllvimEN8b7jXrwqOf-v5A_CdpgnVfiiMM&#38;r=aJN_B9lxV3XtoOYQqya_Bpi9ZKtvuy549O8avEZxzXs&#38;m=Rc7R0N-0O8dJS1R0h99qNS10uYJA1v_dXeFVdgp71fE&#38;s=j38_kYCF6Jer06vbpAMLko-hKZj7SVnEu38MpfpEdsk&#38;e=\">41% of grads end up in roles that don’t require a degree</a>. With COVID-19 hitting young workers particularly hard, this figure is set to rise unless we embrace new approaches, including professional apprenticeships. In creating a direct and meaningful career pathway for young adults, they can help businesses close skills gaps and hit their much-vaunted diversity targets.</p>\n<p>There’s no single solution to these challenges. But the professional apprenticeship can be education’s biggest contribution.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=Y7HfAc2A-6I:KjQUbNx0m84:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a 01:35:21","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:21","title":"To sell or not to sell: Lessons from a bootstrapped CEO","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2142456","description":"<div class=\"article__contributor-byline-wrapper\">\n<div class=\"article__contributor-byline\">\n\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__contributor\">\n\t\t<div class=\"byline__author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span aria-labelledby=\"title\">\n\t\t<title>Share on Twitter</title>\n\t\t<path d=\"M20,4c-0.7,0.3-1.5,0.6-2.4,0.7c0.9-0.5,1.5-1.4,1.8-2.3c-0.8,0.5-1.7,0.8-2.6,1C16.1,2.5,15,2,13.8,2c-2.3,0-4.1,1.9-4.1,4.2c0,0.3,0,0.7,0.1,1C6.4,7,3.4,5.4,1.4,2.9C1,3.5,0.8,4.1,0.8,4.9c0,1.4,0.7,2.7,1.8,3.5C2,8.4,1.4,8.2,0.8,7.9v0.1c0,2,1.4,3.7,3.3,4.1c-0.4,0.1-0.7,0.2-1.1,0.2c-0.3,0-0.5,0-0.8-0.1c0.5,1.7,2,2.9,3.8,2.9c-1.4,1.1-3.2,2-5.1,2c-0.3,0-0.7,0-1-0.1c1.8,1.2,4,1.7,6.3,1.7c7.5,0,11.7-6.4,11.7-12V6.1C18.8,5.6,19.4,4.8,20,4z\"/>\t</svg>\n\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\tGlen Rabie is co-founder and CEO of <a href=\"https://www.yellowfinbi.com\">Yellowfin</a>, a global analytics and BI software vendor.\t</div>\n\t\n\t</div>\n</div><p id=\"speakable-summary\">The clock begins ticking on a startup the day the doors open. Regardless of a young company’s struggles or success, sooner or later the question of when, how or whether to sell the enterprise presents itself. It’s possibly the biggest question an entrepreneur will face.</p>\n<p>For founders who self-funded (bootstrapped) their startup, a boardroom full of additional factors come into play. Some are the same as for investor-funded firms, but many are unique.</p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--left\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\tPut happiness at the center of the decision, and let your intuition — the instincts that made you the person you are today — be your guide.\t\t\t\t\t</blockquote>\n\t</div>\n\t</p>\n<p>After 18 years of bootstrapping a BI software firm into a business that now serves 28,000 companies and three million users in 75 countries, here’s what I’ve learned about myself, my company, about entrepreneurship and about when to grab for that brass ring.</p>\n<h2>Profitable or bust</h2>\n<p>Starting a software company 7,900 miles southwest of Silicon Valley requires some forethought and not a small amount of crazy. When we opened, it didn’t occur to us that one could have an idea and then go knock on someone’s door and ask for money.</p>\n<p>Bootstrapping forced us to be a bit more creative about how we would go about building our company. In the early days, it was a distraction to growth, because we were doing other revenue-generating activities like consulting, development work, whatever we could find to keep ourselves afloat while we built Yellowfin. It meant we couldn’t be 100% focused on our idea.</p>\n<p>However, it also meant we had to generate income from our new company from Day One — something funded companies don’t have to do. We never got into the mindset that it was okay to burn lots of cash and then cross our fingers and hope that it worked.<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=Z7SB1MnficA:SmHhRVkQ4h0:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a 01:35:21","updatedTime":"2021-04-24 01:35:21","title":"Introvoke raises $2.7M to power online events that can be embedded anywhere","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2142996","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">While there&#8217;s been plenty of attention and money lavished on virtual event platforms over the past year, <a href=\"https://www.introvoke.com\">Introvoke</a> co-founder and CEO Oana Manolache predicted that we&#8217;re only at the beginning of a &#8220;third wave of digital transformation.&#8221;</p>\n<p>In her framing, the first wave came at the beginning of the pandemic, when everyone was using video conferencing tools like Zoom for their virtual events. Next came conference platforms like Hopin (which has been <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/04/hopin-confirms-400m-raise-at-5-65b-valuation/\">raising money at a mind-boggling clip</a>). But Manolache argued that even Hopin represents a &#8220;Band-Aid&#8221; that customers are hoping will tide them over until in-person events can resume — particularly when organizers have to point attendees to a third-party platform.</p>\n<p>&#8220;One size does not fit all,&#8221; she said. &#8220;The Band-Aid solution that was only supposed to last for a couple months has had big benefits as companies grew their customer base and revenue targets. Now we&#8217;ve reached the third wave, as organizations want to bring solutions to their own universe and own their relationship with the audience.&#8221;</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>San Francisco-based Introvoke is a Techstars Accelerator graduate aiming to provide this third-wave solution. It&#8217;s announcing today that it has raised $2.7 million in funding led by Struck Capital, while Comcast, Social Leverage, Great Oaks, V1vc, Time CTO Bharat Krish and Resy co-founder Mike Montero also participated.</p>\n<p>The startup offers components like virtual stages, chat rooms and networking hubs, all customizable and embeddable on a customer&#8217;s website. Manolache said Introvoke (the name comes from the idea of &#8220;thought-provoking introductions&#8221;) is designed for a hybrid future, which will take multiple forms: &#8220;Hybrid is going to mean virtual-only events, in-person only events and events that have in-person and<span class=\"Apple-converted-space\"> virtual elements.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2143138\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2143138\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2143138\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_3806.jpeg?w=680\" alt=\"Introvoke\" width=\"680\" height=\"507\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_3806.jpeg 1000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_3806.jpeg?resize=150,112 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_3806.jpeg?resize=300,224 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_3806.jpeg?resize=768,573 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_3806.jpeg?resize=680,507 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_3806.jpeg?resize=50,37 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2143138\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Introvoke</p></div></p>\n<p>Introvoke charges customers based on live event minutes, a model that it says is accessible to companies large and small. Its components can be embedded on websites built with WordPress, Squarespace, Wix, Splash and other platforms, but also on a customer&#8217;s internal intranet.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;ve been so impressed by the way customers are using the technology — conferences, career fairs, employee engagements,&#8221; Manolache said.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"PWiR8eXG4f\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/14/3-best-practices-that-will-maximize-the-value-of-your-online-events/\">These best practices maximize the value of your online events</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;These best practices maximize the value of your online events&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/14/3-best-practices-that-will-maximize-the-value-of-your-online-events/embed/#?secret=PWiR8eXG4f\" data-secret=\"PWiR8eXG4f\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>She added that as customers like Comcast, Wharton and Ritual Motion have used the platform in private preview mode, they&#8217;re beginning to break free of the in-person model. For example, Introvoke events can allow for attendees to chat with each other over weeks or months, not just a few days.</p>\n<p>In a statement, Struck Capital founder and Managing Partner Adam B. Struck suggested that virtual events &#8220;will continue far beyond the COVID-19 pandemic.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;Right now, virtual experiences, from conferences and concerts to company all-hands, are generally hosted on third party platforms, which creates a disjointed experience for the brand or organization hosting the event,&#8221; he continued. &#8220;Virtual enablement should be native to the website and platform of the enterprise itself, and it’s the role of technologists like the <span class=\"il\">Introvoke</span> team to make these experiences as seamless as any in-person event.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"bq6w95T30M\"><p><a
